(Nanjing) The National Government issued an order on the 23rd stating: "Sichuan Province, with its abundant natural resources and rich deposits of forests, minerals, rivers, and lakes, is nevertheless plagued by financial difficulties, continuous warfare, and a chaotic political situation, causing the people to suffer. The government is concerned about the people's hardships and has long understood the root causes. The primary cause is the evil system of military districts. Therefore, there was the order for rectification in the seventeenth year, intending to take advantage of the establishment of the provincial government to establish a plan to allow the people to rest. All measures, including reducing the army, reducing taxes, eliminating military districts, clearly ordering officials to take office, prohibiting the minting of currency, preparing for autonomy, promoting education, supporting local militias, and respecting the judiciary, are all being undertaken to show the minimum measures required and to establish the initial basis for improving Sichuan's administration. If, at this time, the leaders of all armies had a heart of compassion for the starving and drowning people and possessed the desire to save them, then there would be no need to worry about a lack of sincerity and no reason to reopen suspicions. Moreover, given the rich resources and abundant deposits of Sichuan Province, as well as the urgent need to manage various construction projects in civil affairs, politics, education, water conservancy, electricity, and transportation, even if all the talents in Sichuan were gathered and exerted their utmost efforts, there would still be concerns that local human resources would be insufficient or wealth would be left untapped in the mountains and forests. What need is there for distinctions between large and small military districts or disputes over lucrative stationing locations? It is regrettable that those in power are limited by their close associates and are ignorant of the long-term situation. The strong use mergers to expand their military preparations, while the weak exhaust the people's strength to resist. Some hold sway over one area, while others occupy checkpoints to seize profits. Gradually, local militias are absorbed, and local industries are destroyed. The variety of tax names has become endlessly bizarre, and the cruelty of forced loans and advance levies has spread to remote areas. Recently, disregarding the national crisis, they have used the pretext of war to engage in internal strife. The military has sacrificed its elite due to internal warfare, and the common people have been smeared with blood on the battlefield. Alas, my people of Sichuan, are they not to have a day of relief? Although there are not lacking those with a heart for governance and commendable plans, they are inevitably constrained by the environment, leading to suspicion and animosity, and ultimately falling into a situation of mutual harm. This cycle repeats itself endlessly. The waxing and waning of military districts never ceases, and the national foundation and the people's strength are on the verge of irreparable loss. Moreover, at this time of converging disasters and urgent national crisis, the humiliation of enemy invasion is unbearable. The government is not prioritizing the defense against foreign aggression or the settlement of refugees, but only engaging in internal warfare and prioritizing the accumulation of wealth. Even if victorious, it is not martial; even if wealthy, it is not benevolent. If, due to a minor disagreement, a wildfire is ignited, then the impact will affect the very foundation of the nation. Even if the leaders of the various armies are provoked by a moment of passion, they should not remain indifferent to the great plan of national security and survival. The government, entrusted by the party and the nation and bearing the heavy expectations of the people, is constantly planning to rescue the people from their suffering. Now, hearing that the situation in Chengdu and Chongqing is worsening daily, with internal strife escalating, the military is passing through, and the flames of war are spreading, turning cities and villages into ashes and the old and weak into ditches. The people, burdened with unbearable burdens, are suffering such great calamity, like adding depth to water and fuel to fire. Every time we think of this, we cannot help but feel deeply saddened. Therefore, we specially reiterate the order to rectify Sichuan's administration in the seventeenth year, instructing the Executive Yuan to detail the implementation measures and ensure that they are effectively implemented within the shortest possible time. All the military leaders and administrative commissioners in Sichuan should possess a deep understanding of the overall situation, understand the government's heart for saving Sichuan and the nation, observe the plight of the displaced and impoverished people, take responsibility and make mutual concessions, immediately stop the fighting, and strive to move forward in accordance with the Yuan's established measures to usher in a new beginning. The government's duty lies in considering the obedience or disobedience of the various armies as the standard of compliance or defiance. Let each of them respectfully comply and not disobey. This order is of utmost importance." (23rd Central News Agency dispatch)

(Hankou) Regarding the cessation of hostilities in Sichuan: 1) The conflict between Liu and Tian in Chengdu completely stopped on the afternoon of the 20th. The troops of Tian Songyao's division inside the city completely withdrew from the North Gate on the 22nd, preparing to retreat to Tongchuan. The Tian army suffered heavy casualties during the three days and nights of fierce fighting, with the main force losing sixty to seventy percent of its strength. Tian's position in the provincial capital is unstable, and there are rumors of his voluntary resignation. 2) The provincial Liu's troops in the Fulu Zinei area have safely arrived at the designated locations in Xufu and Jiading after receiving orders to retreat, without any loss of strength. 3) Public security in the provincial capital has been restored, but the vitality has been greatly damaged. Liu Wen-hui has initiated fundraising for relief efforts. More than one hundred representatives from gentry, merchants, and public organizations have arrived, and more than ten measures have been discussed and decided for rescuing refugees and various post-war arrangements. Liu Wen-hui and the various generals have all donated large sums of money. (23rd special dispatch)

(Hankou) Deng Xihou telegraphed on the 19th that both Liu and Tian Songyao, Yang Sen, Li Jiayu, and Luo Zezhou advocated that all parties immediately cease military actions, discuss the date of the meeting, and properly discuss the major guidelines and detailed items, with military force as a shield and diplomacy as the priority, so that the sound of weapons will not be heard in the homeland again. Current Commentary

Diplomatic Battle Outside Geneva

— You Xuan

I. × × × ×

The Sino-Japanese diplomatic battle in Geneva has officially unfolded on the 21st of this month. Japan's written opinion on the League of Nations' investigation report was also released on the same day. Our national newspapers have also issued stern rebuttals. Japanese public opinion, under the direction of its military, misunderstands the facts and makes frivolous attacks against our country. As stated in the conclusion of Chapter 5 of said opinion, "Firstly, China is mired in anarchic chaos. Secondly, it cannot guarantee the lives and property of foreigners. Thirdly, it implements an anti-foreign policy, of which Japan is the biggest victim. Fourthly, Japan has an unparalleled special position in Manchuria. Fifthly, Manchurian officials infringe upon Japan's rights and interests. Sixthly, the September 18th Incident arose out of self-defense. Seventhly, Manchuria's independence was a spontaneous action of the people, and the Qing restoration was merely its guiding force." As for the true value of the above opinions, it does not require the estimation of wise men or experts; it is already clearly displayed before us. It uses the excuse that China cannot guarantee the lives and property of foreigners and implements an anti-foreign policy to stir up the feelings of various countries, but the facts are there, and it is difficult to erase them with a single word. Regarding the Northeast, it even fabricated the Wanbaoshan Incident and the Nakamura Incident as a starting point for its implementation of an aggressive policy. Moreover, on the day of the September 18th Incident, the Second Division of the Multiple Gates was far away in Sendai, yet it appeared in Changchun; its Twentieth Division, originally stationed in Longnan, Korea, also attacked our Liaoning at the same time. Therefore, what Japan calls "self-defense" is merely another name for aggression and exclusive occupation. What else could it be? As for the "Manzhou" independence, it disguises itself as a spontaneous national action. Even Sir Lytton, dispatched by Great Britain, who had once been an ally of Japan, believes that "the state of Manzhou is actually manipulated by the Japanese army and officials behind the scenes." If the Japanese deny that they are the source of the turmoil, then one must ask what reasonable basis there is for inserting more than six hundred Japanese officials and ten thousand army troops into the organization of the "Manzhou (puppet) state"? Therefore, we have always considered Japan's opinion on the investigation report to be an erasure of the true facts, a false statement of lies, a threat to China with military force, and an intimidation of the League of Nations with dangerous words, yet cleverly disguising it with the name of "maintaining peace in East Asia" and calling it "self-initiated action." Who is it deceiving? It is only enough to numb the Japanese, who are fanatical about militarism.

II. × × × ×

As for the speech of Japanese representative Yosuke Matsuoka at the special meeting of the League of Nations Administrative Council, it was still nothing more than a repetition of the above opinions, strengthening the tone of stirring up the ill feelings of the great powers towards China, believing that the Chinese national movement was entirely an anti-foreign movement, and focusing on the issue of rejecting Japanese goods. He insisted that the Chinese government was in a leading position in the anti-Japanese goods movement, acting as a cover for its so-called right of self-defense and a smokescreen for its aggression in the three northeastern provinces. At the same time, he further cited four points, such as "national sentiment, delay in time, fear of the deterioration of the situation, and natural means," as statements against entrusting the Northeast dispute to the League of Nations for judgment. Furthermore, he covered up left and right, saying that Japan did not want to go to war with any country, had no territorial ambitions, and was not an aggressive country. In summary, in reality, it was nothing more than wanting to use excuses to delay in order to achieve its aggression against China. Try reading the four reasons stated by Tamaki Hanzawa, the spokesperson for the military, in the article "Hoping for the League of Nations" in the late November issue of the Diplomatic Times. First, he advocated postponing the resolution of the Northeast issue. Second, he advised the League of Nations to wait and see. Matsuoka's arguments are also like this. If Japan really did not want war, then why was the military expenditure for the 1933 budget more than 50% of the total annual expenditure? If Japan had not invaded Manchuria, why were there 100,000 Japanese army troops stationed within the three northeastern provinces? If Japan had no territorial ambitions, why were there more than six hundred Japanese officials in the puppet state? Furthermore, the number of Japanese residents stationed in the three northeastern provinces was only over 200,000. Why does it take one soldier to protect two overseas Chinese? What is more uneconomical and stupid in the world than this? The saying of self-defense, such as self-organization to resist Japan's military aggression, still does not lose its solemn meaning and is in line with the actions of public reason and justice.

III. × × × ×

Well said, Mr. Wellington Koo's words! "...When Japan groundlessly invades Chinese territory, are Sino-Japanese relations still friendly? China certainly wants to seek a peaceful solution through the League of Nations, but China feels that it is necessary to stop the continuous advance of aggressive troops whenever possible. China chooses this form of passive resistance, which is more humane... It is also sufficient to see the characteristic of the Chinese government's tolerant and moderate policy... Japan began to invade the three northeastern provinces... Under the current situation, the Chinese government will legislate to resist Japanese merchants and Japanese goods, and it is not unreasonable to formulate and implement more advanced methods of boycott..." This has indeed shown that our country's moderate tolerance has reached its extreme. No country can give way any further. And I am afraid that a bloody war has already spread throughout East Asia. Moreover, the act of boycotting Japanese goods came after the September 18th Incident, and the anti-Japanese goods movement belongs to the automatic behavior of the people. Whenever a country's political party is truly supported by the people, it is its duty to lead the people to resist foreign aggression, not just a peaceful boycott of goods. Even fighting with iron and blood is inevitable. Otherwise, when the enemy comes, the people will rise up to resist, which is even more natural and natural. What is unfortunate is that our country's resistance to Japanese goods has not been thoroughly implemented, so as to fight a long-term decisive battle with the enemy.

IV. × × × ×

Foreign Minister Luo Wengan believes that "Su Bingwen's anti-Japanese volunteer army is better than the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' thousands of protests and declarations..."

This is indeed a sharp and painful remark. At this time, our country lost 3,767,700 square miles of land, and more than 30 million people suffered the trampling of iron hooves. It is easy to see how weak it is to express its moderate protest with just a "boycott movement." The Japanese still do not repent, but insist on their militarist aggression and still clamor for false debates to decorate their wickedness. Our Chinese people have always loved peace and will never be willing to engage in bloody battles until they are at the end of their rope. However, Japanese militarists repeatedly force each other, having already invaded Liaoning and Jilin, and then disturbing Northern Manchuria. The prosperous Zhabei was turned into a rubble field under Japanese military aircraft. If this can be tolerated, what power is left to survive in the world? Therefore, the strong men between the Black Mountain and the White Water, unwilling to be deceived, suddenly rise up among the fields and fight a desperate battle with the enemy. Although they have not been able to fight back with real iron fists and urge them to find their way, the nation's century-old consciousness of struggle has been deeply rooted in the hearts of the people. Even a million troops cannot uproot it. In terms of political form, there are still many weaknesses, but the people's centripetal force has indeed become increasingly concentrated and gradually gathered its strength. Even in terms of the Northeast Volunteer Army, in the bitter struggle of being besieged on all sides, they fell one after another, causing the Japanese Empire, which is extremely organized and militarily strong, to inevitably become flustered. Isn't the support of strength a lesson of fact?

National diplomacy is especially important at this critical moment. Although Japan is doing its best to implement its delaying policy and put our diplomacy with the League of Nations in a more difficult situation, we also know that the League of Nations may not have the strength to restrain Japan's atrocities. However, the use of diplomacy is ultimately indispensable. Diplomatic negotiations and compromises are essential. Our representatives have already done their best in the peaceful struggle, and our people should prepare their strength as a diplomatic support. In particular, we must use practical efforts to open up new paths for the future.

The volunteer army at Qingduizi Station on the Beining Railway destroys the railway tracks

Engaged in a fierce battle with the Japanese army for a moment

(Beiping) More than 100 members of the volunteer army recently destroyed more than ten feet of railway tracks at Qingduizi on the Beining Railway, attempting to overturn the Fengshan Railway train. A Japanese garrison team happened to be patrolling in an armored car, opened fire when they arrived here, and engaged in a fierce battle with the volunteer army. The volunteer army then retreated towards Shuangtaizi. The pseudo-Fengshan Railway train was four hours late before arriving at Yuguan. Rumors are rife in Yuguan. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

Lin Zhengguo's division firmly defends the Niuzhuang area

Now, more than three months later, it is recently learned that the Japanese army plans to launch a large-scale attack to eliminate the volunteer army in the Yingkou and Haicheng areas. Lin Zheng is preparing to resist. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

Liu Zhennian's division's first batch leaves Yantai and Dalian by boat to Wenzhou

Troops stationed in Ye County board ships behind the Hai Temple north of the city

Lishui County residents request the withdrawal of the order to transfer Liu's division to Zhejiang

(Qingdao) Approximately 6,000 soldiers from the 456th Regiment of the Second Brigade of Liu Zhennian's division, along with 18 mortars and more than 500 mules and horses, boarded five ships—Sheng'an, Taishun, Tonghua, Yuji, and Xinfeng—led by Brigade Commander Liang, and left Yantai for Wenzhou at 6:00 AM on the 23rd. These ships have already departed and will need to return to Yantai once more. Liu returned to Yexian from Laiyang on the 22nd. The First Brigade has already advanced from Ye towards Yantai. Xiong Bin arrived in Qingdao from Jinan on the evening of the 23rd at 11:00 PM to meet with Shen. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

(Jinan) Zhang Chucai, chief of staff of the Yantai Command, reported to Shen Honglie in a telegram dated the 21st, saying that in order to represent your position, inspect the suffering of the people, and investigate the actual situation of the 21st Division, he passed through Yongfuyuan to the vicinity of Fushan City. What he saw and heard is reported as follows: 1) Travelers and merchants on the Yantai-Weifang line can pass without hindrance. The number of military vehicles and horses along the way is slightly more than 500, making way one after another, with guards stationed at intersections. 2) Villagers in each village said that the discipline of the 21st Division is strict and definitely different from before. They all thanked your position for the compromise and reconciliation. The Second Brigade, which camped in Zhuqi Village, all brought their own dry food, and the people only provided porridge, without entering the people's homes or asking for anything. The same is true of the cavalry regiment stationed in Fushan City. Near Yongfuyuan, because there is no defense zone on our side, there are no stationed troops. 3) The Second Brigade all gathered on the beach early in the morning for training, and the combat troops seemed to be definitely more than 6,000. 4) Two transport ships have already docked at the pier and loaded luggage and more than 40 horses, which have arrived at Zhuqi Village. It is heard that they will be transported onto the ship immediately, but the departure may be on the evening of the 22nd, because the luggage is mostly difficult to load. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 23rd)

(Beiping) Zhang Shaotang telegraphed Ping, saying that Liu Zhennian had returned to Ye from Laiyang, and the entire Second Brigade of Liu's troops boarded the ships. The ships set sail at noon on the 23rd and headed for Fujian and Zhejiang. The remaining ships are waiting for the arrival of the baggage and will then sail south. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

(Beiping) Song Shishan and Gao Lingbai telegraphed Jiang Bocheng, saying that Liang Lizhu's brigade of Liu's troops boarded ships in Yantai this morning and sailed to the two counties of Yichu in eastern Zhejiang. Jiaodong will be taken over by Cao Fulin's division. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

(Jinan) For the sake of speeding up the transfer of Liu Zhennian's troops, in addition to those who have arrived in Yantai and boarded the ships from Yantai, those in Ye will board the ships behind the Hai Temple, 18 li north of Yecheng. Because the water there is shallow, seagoing ships cannot dock, and soldiers and baggage are all transported by small boats from the shore and then transferred to seagoing ships. It is heard that Zhang Luanji's independent brigade of Liu's troops has already departed, leaving only two regiments in Ye. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

(Jinan) Xiong Bin left Ye for Jinan this morning. This afternoon at 5:00 PM, he took the Jiaoji No. 4 train to Qingdao to meet with Shen Honglie. (Hangzhou) Liu Zhennian telegraphed the Lishui County government in Zhejiang, ordering them to raise 25,000 bags of flour, 600,000 catties of rice, 6 million catties of straw, and several million catties of coal. The county's party headquarters and public groups said that the county's territory is less than 100 li, and Liu's request is nearly one million yuan, which is not enough to supply even half of the county's annual production. The people are panicking and telegraphed the province on the 23rd, begging Jiang to withdraw the order to transfer to Zhejiang. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

Chairman Chiang approves adding disaster relief donations to railway and telegraph charges

To fund post-disaster recovery in recovered bandit areas of three provinces

(Nanjing) Chiang telegraphed the Executive Yuan, approving the previous telegram from Shi Ying, Wang Zhen, Wang Xiaolai, and others, stating that the recovered bandit areas in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui urgently needed disaster relief and that the government should add disaster relief donations to railway and telegraph charges. After separate review, the following conclusions were reached: 1. Originally requested that a disaster relief donation be added to long-distance railway passenger tickets nationwide: 4 jiao for first-class, 2 jiao for second-class, and 1 jiao for third-class. It is proposed to follow this for first-class, change second-class to 3 jiao, and change third-class to 5 fen. Third-class passenger tickets are financially weaker, and ticket prices have been repeatedly increased in recent years. Calculated as a percentage, the increase is already higher than first-class and second-class, and it is not appropriate to increase it further. 2. Originally requested that a disaster relief donation be added to freight on the Pinghan Railway: 5% for salt and coal, and 2% for other goods. Upon investigation, Pinghan freight is currently dispersed by the Longhai Line and Huaiyun, and the commerce of Hankou is declining, which is one of the reasons. It is not appropriate to increase freight charges further, which would hinder freight transportation. Moreover, in order to develop the rural economy of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, it is necessary to reduce freight charges to facilitate the circulation of agriculture. This item should not be discussed. 3. Originally requested that a disaster relief donation be added to telegrams, regardless of wired or wireless, distance, at 5 fen per telegram. Upon investigation, adding donations to telegrams has little connection with the livelihoods of ordinary people and seems to be feasible. 4. Originally requested that the additional donation be set for a period of six months, which is not too long and seems to be feasible. However, it should be stated that it should be revoked immediately upon the expiration of the limit. The above measures are forwarded to the Control Yuan for review and are to be separately ordered to the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications to follow. Please investigate and reply. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

After discussion, the Foreign Affairs Committee decides to instruct the delegation

To state to the League of Nations that the report should be submitted to the General Assembly

(Nanjing) The Foreign Affairs Committee held a meeting on the evening of the 23rd. Regarding the Japanese side's unwillingness to submit the report to the League of Nations General Assembly, it decided to instruct the Geneva delegation by telegram to state to the League of Nations, in accordance with the final paragraph of Article 15 of the League of Nations Covenant, that it must be submitted to the General Assembly. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

He Minhun's troops fiercely attack Taonan

Engaging in fierce battles with the enemy along the Siping-Taonan Railway for two days and nights

Brigade Commander Lu bravely kills the enemy, taking a stray bullet in his arm

(Beiping) Wang Yunping, the military affairs commissioner of the Rehe National Anti-Japanese Army, and Li Siru, the military affairs commissioner and commander-in-chief of the Second Route Army, jointly telegraphed Yan Bewei, the military affairs commissioner and representative stationed in Shanghai, yesterday, reporting on a section of the battle situation. The text is as follows: Extremely urgent telegram to Brother Yan Bewei, representative of the Rehe National Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army, and forwarded to Chairman He Junjian, I have just received a telegram from our division commander Liu Jiashan, stating that our army has been fighting at Hongxing Shuanggang on the Siping-Taonan Railway for days since occupying Zhanyu. On the 19th, in response to a telegram from Commander Su Bingwen, we urgently attacked Taonan to join forces at Ang'angxi to relieve the siege of Fularji. We immediately ordered our Lu Wenjiong Brigade to advance north at full speed. At dawn on the 20th, we were surrounded by enemy marine corps, mountain artillery units, armored vehicle units, and air force units. Fortunately, our Brigade Commander Lu took the lead, and all officers and soldiers were exceptionally brave, engaging in fierce battles with the enemy for two days and nights. Only this morning, the 22nd, did we defeat the enemy. It is estimated that in this battle, the enemy suffered more than 600 casualties, and we suffered more than 300 casualties. Brigade Commander Lu was hit by a stray bullet in his arm. Now, due to a change in strategy, we have withdrawn from Zhanyu to Gaoliban and plan to counterattack after replenishing ammunition. We are jointly reporting this and hope that you will forward it to the General Seat, urging him to go north as soon as possible to preside over everything. Brother Li Siru and Wang Yunping kowtow. (United Press dispatch from the 23rd)

US Minister Johnson arrives in Beijing

(Nanjing) Johnson answers questions from guests: 1) I am coming to Beijing because I have been away from Beijing for a long time, and the League of Nations Administrative Council is currently in session. There are still matters concerning Sino-American relations that need to be discussed with your country's Ministry of Foreign Affairs. 2) Regarding the rumors of an international committee, I have not yet received an official report, and I do not know how the committee will be organized or what its powers will be. Therefore, I am unable to express my opinion. 3) The Democratic Party won the election in the United States this time, but its traditional foreign policy, such as on the Far East issue, will definitely not change. Regarding the resumption of diplomatic relations with Russia, it will have to wait until Roosevelt takes office as president next April to consider and decide. 4) There are very few American residents in the Northeast. Since the incident of the murder of an American resident last month, they have all moved into cities to avoid the impact of the unrest. I plan to return to Ping before Christmas on December 25th. The Consulate General Peck is in the capital as my representative, and there will be no inconvenience in negotiations. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

Central Political Council

Decides to have the Executive Yuan and the Military Council handle the construction of the auxiliary capital and the temporary capital

Orders the Ministry of Finance to draft a tariff law and submit it to the Legislative Yuan

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 333rd meeting on the morning of the 23rd, presided over by Ju Zheng. The following important cases were resolved: 1) The Central Executive Committee transferred the proposal of Chiang Kai-shek and others to construct Xi'an as the auxiliary capital and Luoyang as the temporary capital. Resolution: (1) The first section of establishing a direct administrative yuan in the auxiliary capital is to be reviewed by eleven commissioners, including Wu Jingheng and Zhang Ji. (2) The sections on the construction of the temporary capital are generally approved and handed over to the Executive Yuan Military Council to properly formulate measures and proceed quickly. 2) The Finance Group reported on the review of the Shanghai, Beiping, Shandong, and other chambers of commerce's request to quickly determine the tariff law. It was considered that China's tariffs are already autonomous, and a tariff law should be formulated. It is proposed to quickly order the Ministry of Finance to draft a tariff law and submit it to the council for approval in principle and then hand it over to the Legislative Yuan for review. As for the request for relief for merchants and people who do not comply with the tax customs' punishments before the tariff law is promulgated, the tax customs are one of the central government agencies, and merchants and people who do not comply with its punishments may file a complaint with the Ministry of Finance in accordance with the provisions of the Petition Law. Is this appropriate? Please vote. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinion. 3) Approved the establishment of a temporary municipal council in Nanjing. 4) Approved several budget cases for various agencies. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

(Nanjing) Wu Jingheng proposed to the Central Political Council today to retain the existing address of the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government in the temporary capital, and it has been resolved and passed. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

(Nanjing) At the Central Political Council on the morning of the 23rd, Zhu Jiahua gave a detailed report on the case of Chen Fumu and Li Guojie privately mortgaging the assets of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Various commissioners proposed to order Chen's arrest. After discussion, it was decided to handle it in accordance with the resolution of the Executive Yuan and hand it over to the court. If Chen fails to appear in court at the appointed time, the government will issue an arrest warrant. (Special dispatch from the 23rd)

National General Budget for the 21st Year

(Nanjing) The national general budget for the 21st year, regarding expenditures, has been repeatedly reduced by the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics and is now close to the total revenue. However, due to the severity of the national crisis and the particular importance of military affairs, military expenditure still accounts for over 47% of the total expenditure. Debt service accounts for over 25%, while financial affairs and subsidies each account for over 8%. Education and cultural expenses account for over 2%. National affairs and foreign affairs each account for over 1%. Construction, party affairs, industry, internal affairs, justice, Mongolian and Tibetan affairs, etc., all account for less than 1%. (23rd Special Dispatch)

A Scandal in Changchun

Rumor of Pu Yi Wanting to Take a Japanese Concubine

=Instigation by Zheng Xiaoxu and his son=

=Pu's Wife, Rong, Becomes Ill with Anger=

=Ronglu Invites His Wife to Persuade Her=

Recently, Pu Yi in Beiping, under the instigation of Zheng Xiaoxu and his son, and introduced by Xie Jieshi, desired to take a Japanese woman as a concubine. This was discovered by Pu's wife, Rong, who strongly argued against it with Pu. Pu, at a loss, sought advice from Zheng, Xie, and others. Zheng and the others said that the ruler's command should not be disobeyed, and urged Pu to quickly take the woman. Rong discovered this again, and when Zheng entered to see Pu Yi, she scolded Zheng fiercely, insisting on dragging him back to Beiping together. Zheng retreated in embarrassment. Pu's concubine was excessively angered and has contracted a serious illness. Despite repeated treatments by famous doctors, she has not recovered. Her father, Ronglu, unable to persuade her effectively, telegraphed his wife in Beiping, summoning her to go and dissuade Rong. Ronglu's wife departed for Tanggu last night to transfer to a ship to Dalian, and then on to Changchun to mediate. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Japanese Ships Operating Illegally in Inland Waters

(Nanjing) The inspection of ships operating in inland waters has been handled by the Maritime Administration Bureau since its establishment, having been transferred from the customs. Regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign shipping companies, they should comply with the regulations and undergo inspection. A certain Japanese company's small ship is operating in inland waters and intentionally does not comply with the regulations, leading to the local customs refusing to clear it. The Japanese Consulate in Nanjing has sent a letter to the Maritime Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications to negotiate. The reply stated that such matters should be handled through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Recently, the Vice-Consul of the Japanese Consulate mentioned this matter to the newly appointed Director of the Maritime Administration Department, Gao. Gao replied in a private conversation that diplomatic matters should still be handled through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. As for ships operating in inland waters, regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, they should obtain a certificate from the Maritime Administration Bureau to ensure the uniformity of maritime administration. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Dutch Authorities in the Netherlands East Indies Suppress Overseas Chinese

(Nanjing) According to news from returned overseas Chinese, the authorities in the British and Dutch colonies in the South Seas used to collect an entry tax of 50 guilders per overseas Chinese person. Later, this was increased to 75 guilders, then to 100 guilders. Last year, it was increased to 170 guilders, and recently it has been increased to 250 guilders. This is a plan by the Dutch authorities to suppress overseas Chinese. In the past four years, the entry tax has increased several times. If the diplomatic authorities do not make vigorous efforts to find a solution, it is feared that it will become increasingly difficult for our people to go to the Dutch colonies in the future. (23rd Special Dispatch)

There are Claims that the World Economic Conference has Invited Chinese Representatives to Participate

Hoover Argues that the Conference Should Discuss the Silver Issue

China's Economic Stability is Related to the World Economy

▲ National News Agency, Geneva, 22nd: Today, there are many sources here who believe that the decision by the organizing committee of the World Economic Conference to invite Chinese experts to participate in the preparations is merely a smokescreen. Its real intention is to include China's economic construction on the agenda of the conference. However, the original proposer, the American representative Davis, who is now in London, denies that his proposal contains any other intentions, saying that it is only because China is the largest silver-using country, and the silver issue may become one of the most important issues of the conference, so Chinese experts should also be invited to join the preparatory personnel. Furthermore, the authorities in charge of the various plans to be discussed at the conference have reportedly declared that the discussion of the silver issue at the conference will have no chance of success. However, experts believe that since U.S. President Hoover has made the discussion of the entire silver issue a condition for the United States to participate in the conference, it will be difficult to exclude the silver issue from the discussion at the conference. In addition, after China's participation, the silver issue will need to be considered further. Other sources also believe that the major powers have agreed that the stability of the Chinese economy will greatly contribute to the progress of the world economy. However, they are unable to explain the reasons for the recent invitation to Chinese experts to prepare, and they are also unclear about the intentions of European experts to oppose the discussion of the silver issue.

▲ Havas News Agency, Geneva, 22nd: The League of Nations Administrative Council has organized a subcommittee to monitor the progress of the preparations for the World Economic Conference. This subcommittee met this morning, chaired by British Foreign Secretary Simon, and resolved to convene all the experts on the preparatory committee for the Economic Conference in January next year to prepare a report to be submitted to the Administrative Council for review. The Economic Conference will be held no sooner than May. Before the conference is held, the preparatory committee may convene again if necessary.

Hoover Indicates Meeting with Roosevelt to Discuss War Debt Issue

Progress Has Been Made as a Result of the Meeting

Meeting with Members of Congress Today

▲ Reuters, Washington, 22nd: At 3:40 this afternoon, President-elect Roosevelt, accompanied by his advisor, Columbia University Professor Melle, went to the White House to meet with President Hoover to discuss the war debt issue. President Hoover sincerely hopes that this meeting can work out a common plan to deal with international financial obligations. The proposals President Hoover intends to submit to Congress will depend on the extent to which Roosevelt agrees to suspend payment of the installments due in December. It is now believed that Hoover advocates suspension. If they can reach an agreement, their power can overcome any opposition in Congress. Treasury Secretary Mills also participated in the meeting. The results of the meeting, which lasted two hours, can only be gleaned from a brief statement that said, "There is a feeling that progress has been made at the meeting." During the meeting, secret service agents guarded all the doors of the meeting room. Tonight, Roosevelt and Vice President-elect Garner will meet with Democratic leaders to discuss the same issue. President Hoover is scheduled to meet with members of Congress tomorrow. Congress has met today to exchange views. It is reported that the Italian government intends to pay the war debt installment of $1,245,000 when it is due. According to the New York Times, Roosevelt will only be a "listener" at the meeting unless he sees a complete process that combines a revised debt management plan with a plan to restore international trade. It is heard that Roosevelt now believes that negotiations with the countries indebted to the United States should include tariffs, or even new agreements on arms reduction.

▲ Havas News Agency, Washington, 22nd: European countries have sent dispatches to the United States requesting permission to defer war debt payments and to reorganize the war debts. Recently, the Czech Ambassador to the United States also submitted a dispatch to the U.S. Secretary of State Stimson in support of other European countries.

▲ National News Agency, Washington, 22nd: President-elect Roosevelt went to the White House today to meet with President Hoover for about two hours. Afterwards, a statement was released to the press, stating briefly that the two presidents met from 3:30 PM to 6:02 PM and discussed the issues raised in previous telegrams in detail and felt that progress had been made. President Hoover will meet with members of Congress tomorrow. It is also reported that Senators Harrison and George, Representatives Rayburn and Collier, and other prominent financiers such as Mr. Baruch will go to the White House tomorrow to meet with the President.

Hitler's Cabinet Formation Plan Fails

The Issue of a Congressional Majority Arises

▲ Reuters, Berlin, 22nd: The contents of President Hindenburg's letter to Hitler are gradually being leaked, and it is believed that Hitler's attempt to appoint himself as Chancellor has failed again. It is heard that after the President received Hitler's answer regarding the formation of a new cabinet, he replied that whoever assumes this position must have a congressional majority. Hitler now feels that it is difficult to decide whether he can assume the cabinet formation based on this condition, but must reply by Thursday night at the latest. Hitler and his aides discussed the matter all day and only dispersed in the evening. Party members only claimed that they are still in contact with the President. In his reply, the President stated that the presidential cabinet cannot be led by the leader of one party, so even if Hitler forms a cabinet, it must be based on Congress. From the appearance of things, Hitler may not be able to obtain a majority, and Papen has a hope of regaining power by the end of this week.

▲ National News Agency, Berlin, 22nd: Leading figures of the National Socialist Party met with reporters tonight. Hitler's final proposal to the President and Hindenburg may not be selected until Wednesday morning. They also said that they believe Hitler does not want to organize a cabinet with a majority in Congress because they believe that such a cabinet cannot last and, at present, it is almost impossible to obtain a majority in Congress.

▲ Havas News Agency, Berlin, 22nd: Hitler has convened the main members of the National Socialist Party and political figures to consider the conditions set by Hindenburg for him. Hitler raised questions about certain points and asked Hindenburg to explain them in detail. Hindenburg's reply was delivered to Hitler this afternoon. The letter will not be published until the political crisis is resolved. As far as we know, Hindenburg replied that a parliamentary cabinet, such as the one Hitler is responsible for organizing, should have the broadest majority party in parliament to avoid being threatened by small parties and can rely on this majority as a backing to implement politics. In this way, it will not be necessary to apply Article 48 of the Constitution again and issue orders in lieu of laws. Hitler also asked intermediaries to inquire whether Hugenberg, the leader of the National Nationalist Party, could join the cabinet he organized as Minister of Public Economics, and stated that the cabinet positions related to politics, such as Chancellor, Interior, and Justice, are reserved for National Socialists. Hugenberg replied that he is unwilling to accept this proposal because after actually joining, he will eventually be squeezed out by the Nazi Party. The National Socialist Party believes that Hugenberg's rejection is intended to put the National Socialist Party in a difficult position. Hitler therefore requested to organize a presidential cabinet that does not purely rely on the majority party in parliament so that he can issue orders in lieu of laws to implement administrative affairs, following the precedents of Brüning and Papen. However, it is feared that Hitler's request will not be satisfied.

German Foreign Minister Holds Meetings with British and American Representatives

▲ National News Agency, Berlin, 22nd: Although the masses' attention is focused on the cabinet crisis, the newspapers still reserve space to publish reports on Foreign Minister Neurath's discussions with diplomats from various countries in Geneva on the possibility of Germany rejoining the Disarmament Conference. However, France is currently in a difficult situation and is not paying much attention to this matter, but is quietly awaiting the results of the discussions.

British Parliament Discusses Unemployment Issue

The Gold Standard is Difficult to Restore in the Short Term

▲ Reuters, London, 22nd: This afternoon, the House of Commons began to discuss the reply to the Queen's speech opening Parliament. Prime Minister MacDonald defended against the opposition party's Lansbury's criticisms of the government's policies, saying that the Labor Party had tried to use relief work to deal with the unemployment problem, but when the cost reached its highest point, the number of unemployed people increased rapidly. The unemployment situation two years ago was worse than it is now. The government should certainly promote various ordinary undertakings belonging to the municipality, but taxes must not be abused. What the government must deal with is that even when trade has recovered to the extent that the people can expect, there will still be no shortage of unemployed people, so this is not a temporary relief problem. The government is still working with the relevant departments to plan measures, with restoring agriculture as the main focus. The percentage of the population that is directly related to agriculture must be greater than when the factory industry is developed. As for external events, the World Economic Conference is currently encountering some obstacles, but the British government is still promoting its early convening. Foreign Secretary Simon has already made a statement on the disarmament issue, and he does not want to repeat it. He believes that the entire House will unanimously trust Simon's efforts for the country in Geneva. Lansbury criticized the government for failing to take immediate measures to relieve unemployment, so the Prime Minister made this reply.

▲ Reuters, London, 22nd: Former Home Secretary Samuel, in a debate in the House of Commons today, mentioned the issue of Britain restoring the gold standard, saying that Britain may be forced by other countries to restore the gold standard at the future economic conference. The current situation is quite dangerous. Britain should certainly stabilize it, but unless international commercial constraints are lifted and the war debt issue is resolved, Britain really cannot do anything. If these two things are not given appropriate attention in advance, then even if Britain restores the gold standard, the result will inevitably be that it will still be forced to abolish it one day.

Japan's Plan to Build a Large Suspension Bridge Over the Kanmon Straits

Construction Cost Requires 30 Million Yuan

According to the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun, transportation between Shimonoseki and Moji, two key locations connecting Honshu and Kyushu, has traditionally relied on ferry services. Recognizing advancements in the times and changes in societal conditions, the government has decided to construct a steel suspension bridge across the Kanmon Straits. In late this month, Interior Ministry official Nagata and his team will conduct on-site surveys, with the surveying period lasting until March or April of next year. The bridge's location is set for the Hayatomo Straits within the Kanmon Straits. The bridge will be 570 ken long and 12 ken wide. Simultaneously, military defenses will be established in the surrounding area, allowing warships to navigate freely under the bridge. The bridge's height will be determined by the highest tide level, approximately 60 feet above sea level. The bridge's structure will be divided into two levels: the first level for trains and the second level for pedestrians, carriages, automobiles, and streetcars, making it a uniquely grand suspension bridge for the entire nation. The total construction cost is estimated at 30 million yuan. Upon completion of the on-site survey, a grand conference of the Interior Ministry, Railway Department, and Army and Navy will be convened to decide on implementation.

▲Reuter's Tokyo, 23rd: The Cabinet has decided to allow Japanese citizens to marry native Taiwanese people. An order to this effect will be issued by Japan shortly.

Important News

Japan in the Storm (Japan Communication)

The Greatest Natural Disaster Since the Earthquake

Houses Collapsed, Cliffs Crumbled

Tokyo Suffered Considerable Damage, Shizuoka Even More

Japan, with its rampant militarism and aggressive ambitions, believes it can intimidate the world, but its internal problems are no lighter than China's. We will address the reasons for this another time; for now, let's discuss the recent natural disaster.

Around 10 p.m. on the 14th of this month, a storm suddenly arose in Tokyo, accompanied by heavy rain. The peaceful city was transformed into something resembling a hellish scene. Streets were deserted, and even the self-proclaimed brave policemen dared not venture out. Electricity was almost entirely cut off. The Asakusa district, normally a land of entertainment with its dazzling decorations and colorful flags, was entirely swept away by the wind and rain. Many roofs of the predominantly wooden houses were torn off. At 10 p.m., just when people were heading to the market, men and women alike were like drenched chickens, unable to return home, exposed to the wind and rain in roofless houses. The Tsukiji area, being low-lying, was also hit by tidal surges, which, although not severe, caused considerable alarm. More than half of the utility poles in the streets were blown down. Over two thousand houses collapsed, and forty-three or forty-four thousand homes were flooded. Over fifteen hundred trees were broken. The worst affected areas were Koishikawa, Kamata, Totsuka, Takata, Nippori, etc. Thirty-six vessels related to the waterways department were lost. Telegraph and telephone lines were down. Tokyo Station was temporarily thrown into chaos. Trains from outside were blocked by the storm and unable to enter the station, while trains already at the station were unable to depart.

According to the Japan Central Meteorological Observatory, the wind speed in Tokyo reached 20 meters per second, three times faster than a 100-meter sprint.

Yokohama fared even worse, with wind speeds reaching 36 meters per second. The extent of the damage was naturally even greater than in Tokyo. In addition, the cliff near the Rinhokan suddenly collapsed, crushing twenty nearby homes, resulting in over twenty deaths and injuries, with over a hundred people buried underneath. Upon receiving this information, the police dispatched capable officers, along with members of the local youth corps and veterans, to carry out rescue operations amidst the fierce wind and rain. With no lights or electricity, the scene was like a battlefield.

The wind and rain damage suffered by eastern Shizuoka Prefecture is said to be even worse than the damage suffered during the great earthquake. Collapsed houses and broken utility poles were more numerous than in Tokyo. A fire broke out in Higashi Kashiwabara near Suzukawa Station, spreading to Naka Kashiwabara and Nishi Kashiwabara, and further to Ono Shinden, burning a total of 350 houses. Over 300 other buildings were almost completely destroyed, barely standing. Seventy or eighty houses also collapsed in Numazu city. Japanese wooden houses with paper windows are difficult to extinguish once they catch fire, and with strong winds, it is even more hopeless. Other prefectures in the Kanto region have suffered similar disasters, but because telegraph and telephone lines are down, no news can be obtained from those areas.

The hardest hit by this storm were the working masses. During the economic crisis, they already had to endure wage cuts and unemployment. Now, officials are saying that the economy is improving, or at least showing signs of improvement. According to the price index published by the Bank of Japan, raw silk prices have risen by 52%, wheat by 67%, and rice prices have remained relatively stable since May. However, American cotton has risen by 135%, Indian cotton by about 80-90%, and soybeans and bean cakes have also increased by over 80%. In short, all necessities (except rice) continue to rise, generally by about 50%. This is what is meant by signs of good business. However, at the same time, the number of unemployed has increased from over 480,000 to over 510,000, not including their dependent families. If the families are included, at least 1.5 million people are suffering from unemployment. Even those who have work are faced with rising prices and a depreciated currency, and their wages have not increased. The general social life has become even more difficult, especially in the areas affected by the storm. Although there was no large-scale loss of life, the loss of collapsed houses adds a heavy burden during a time of crisis, which is a truly bitter situation. Moreover, at least 1.1 billion yen in public debt will be added next year, while farmers are suffering even more from rising prices and falling rice prices. As a result, both extremes of the ideological spectrum are particularly developed, focusing their resentment on the political authorities. Assassination groups are springing up like mushrooms after the rain. Recently, during the grand military exercise (autumn maneuvers), the emperor and military leaders attended, and Prime Minister Saito also went west to participate, and was almost targeted by an assassination group. Fortunately, the police discovered this early and arrested a person at Kyoto Station. The investigation is still ongoing. From this, one can see that the storm's impact is not limited to just one area. (November 17th, Tokyo, Japan)

Legislative Yuan Passes Amendments to the Administrative Execution Law

The Legislative Yuan held its 112th meeting on the morning of the 22nd, passing amendments to the Administrative Execution Law, consisting of 12 articles in total. The full text is recorded below: (Article 1) When necessary, administrative agencies may carry out indirect or direct compulsory measures in accordance with the provisions of this law. (Article 2) Indirect compulsory measures include: 1. Substituted execution; 2. Fines. The measures in the preceding paragraph may not be implemented without prior written warning specifying a time limit, except in cases where substituted execution is deemed to be an emergency. (Article 3) If a person is obligated to act according to law or pursuant to a lawful order but fails to do so, the competent administrative agency may carry out the action or order a third party to carry it out, and collect the expenses from the obligated person. (Article 4) In any of the following circumstances, the competent administrative agency may impose a fine: 1. If a person is obligated to act according to law or pursuant to a lawful order, but fails to do so, and the action cannot be carried out by the agency or a third party; 2. If a person is obligated not to act according to law or pursuant to a lawful order, but acts in violation thereof. (Article 5) The fines in the preceding article are determined according to the following provisions: 1. Ministries of the central government: up to 30 yuan; 2. Provincial governments and their departments, and municipal governments directly under the Executive Yuan and their bureaus: up to 20 yuan; the same applies to administrative agencies directly under the central government ministries and commissions; 3. County and city governments: up to 10 yuan; the same applies to administrative agencies directly under provincial governments and their departments; 4. Other administrative agencies: up to 5 yuan. (Article 6) Direct compulsory measures include: 1. Restraint of a person; 2. Seizure, use, disposition, or restriction of use of property; 3. Intrusion into a residence or other place. (Article 7) Restraint may not be imposed unless one of the following circumstances exists: 1. Insanity or drunkenness rendering the person unable to care for their life and body, and endangering the life and body of others; 2. Intent to commit suicide, where restraint is necessary to save the person's life; 3. Violence or brawling, where restraint is necessary to prevent harm; 4. Other circumstances deemed necessary for rescue or where there is a risk to public safety, and restraint is necessary for rescue or prevention of harm. The restraint in the preceding paragraph may not exceed 24 hours. (Article 8) Weapons, dangerous instruments, and other dangerous items may be seized if seizure is necessary to prevent harm. The seizure in the preceding paragraph may not exceed 30 days, unless otherwise required by law for confiscation or disposal. If the seized item is not claimed within one year, ownership belongs to the national treasury. (Article 9) In the event of natural disasters or incidents, or other situations on transportation, hygiene, or public safety that pose a danger, the land, houses, or goods may be used, disposed of, or have their use restricted if it is not possible to achieve the purpose of protection without using, disposing of, or restricting their use. (Article 10) Intrusion into a residence or other place may not be carried out unless one of the following circumstances exists: 1. The life, body, or property of the people is in imminent danger, and intrusion is necessary for rescue; 2. Gambling or other behaviors that disrupt public morals or public safety are occurring, and intrusion is necessary to stop them. In the circumstances of paragraph 2 above, if it occurs after sunset and before sunrise, the residents should be notified, except for hotels, taverns, tea houses, theaters, and other places where the public enters and exits at night. (Article 11) Administrative agencies may not take direct compulsory measures in the circumstances of Articles 1 and 4 unless they deem indirect compulsory measures impossible or consider it an emergency. (Article 12) This law shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Zhu and Mao Suddenly Flee from the Fujian-Zhejiang Border into Eastern Jiangxi

▲ Attempting to Invade Fuzhou via Jinxi

▲ Mao and Xu's Troops Cut Off the Bandits' Return Route

Nanchang communication: Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, Lin Biao, Dong Zhentang, Luo Binghui and other factions, after gathering on the Jiangxi-Zhejiang-Fujian border and joining forces with Shao Fang in northeastern Jiangxi, are actively moving towards the Zhejiang border, intending to attack western Zhejiang, so that they can freely plunder and solve the problem of supplies. However, the plan agreed upon by the bandit central authorities this time is to circle around the border of the bandit area and conduct guerrilla warfare in the non-bandit area, in order to disturb the large red area and avoid being confined to the barren bandit area, resulting in natural extinction due to economic blockade. According to Fuzhou news, the red bandits' claims of attacking Zhejiang and fleeing to Guangdong are all feints. In fact, the bandits stationed the pseudo-Fifth Army Corps in northwestern Fujian to guard the area, and Peng Dehuai of the pseudo-Third Army Corps gathered in Lichuan, invading Nancheng and Nanfeng, restraining the divisions of Tao Zhiyue, Li Yunjie, Xu Kesun, and Lian Zhong in the two Nans. Another faction, Lin Biao of the pseudo-First Army Corps, Xiao Ke of the pseudo-Twelfth Army, and a part of Luo Binghui of the pseudo-Twenty-second Army, suddenly attacked Zixi and Jinxi via Guangze to peep at Fuzhou. Yesterday, military sources also reported that there were few troops stationed in Zixi and Jinxi, and both were harassed by bandits in the past two days, and they moved down the Lin (chuan)-Jin (xi) highway. The bandits' vanguard has already advanced to Xuchuan, dozens of miles away from Linchuan. Therefore, the situation in Fuzhou is inevitably tense, and residents have also moved to the province to take refuge. However, after receiving news that the bandits had penetrated deep into eastern Jiangxi, the highest military authorities believed that it was a good opportunity to suppress the bandits, which could achieve twice the results with half the effort compared to going deep into the bandit area. At present, the Mao, Li, and Xu divisions in Nancheng and the Zhou Hunyuan troops in Guixi have cut off the bandits' return route from Zixi, Guixi, and the Fujian border, and surrounded them on all sides with the Sun Lianzhong and Wu Qixing troops in Yile, hoping to eliminate the bandits in Jinzi. The air force stationed in the province has been flying reconnaissance and bombing missions over eastern Jiangxi, the Fujian border, and the Jinxi area for days, which has been very effective. (November 22nd)

The Jing-Wu Highway Will Be Completed Soon

▲ Scheduled to Officially Open to Traffic in the Coming Year

▲ Completion of the Anhui Western Transportation Network

Wuhu Communication: Anhui Province's development of commerce and culture has been greatly hindered by traffic congestion in recent years. The inconvenience of military transportation has particularly affected the bandit suppression work. Therefore, officials and the public alike believe that the construction of highways is urgent. The Jing-Wu line is even more pressing because it connects the Shanghai-Hangzhou and Tianjin-Pukou lines. The construction of the Jing-Wu Road has been going on for years, but it was only barely opened from Wuhu to Dangtu last year due to the sluggishness of the project. However, it was not long before the vehicles were suddenly requisitioned and the service was suspended again. It has not been restored until now. Recently, under the supervision of the Anhui Provincial Government and the Tri-Province Bandit Suppression Headquarters, the unfinished projects in Anhui Province were completed day and night. It has now been decided to open to traffic on New Year's Day, 1933. The company contracting the automobile business on the Jing-Wu line is composed of prominent businessmen from Nanjing, Wuhu, and Dangtu. They are currently in the process of signing contracts with the construction departments of Jiangsu and Anhui provinces. Therefore, it is a government-supervised, merchant-operated project. It is said that the plan is to establish large stations in Nanjing, Wuhu, and Dangtu, and small stations along the way. The first step is to prepare six passenger cars and four freight cars, and then expand the business as it develops. After the opening of the line, it is expected that it will only take three hours to travel from Wuhu to Beijing. The convenience of transportation in southern Anhui will be far greater than before.

In western Anhui, since the suppression of the communists in the summer, the inconvenience of transportation has greatly affected military and political affairs. After the arrival of Liang Guanying's 25th Route Army, the engineering team of the Social Service Committee was responsible for planning the transportation network of the counties in western Anhui, allocating rear troops and local people to cooperate in the construction. The Shu-Huo Road (Shucheng to Huoshan), 150 li long, started construction at the end of August and was opened to traffic on September 25th. The Tao-San Road (Taoxi Town to Sanhe Town), 60 li long, started construction in mid-October and was completed at the end of October. The Shu-An Road (Shucheng via Tongcheng to Anqing), 250 li long, had the original roadbed mostly built, but the bridges and culverts were not repaired and it has not been opened to traffic. The department sent personnel to repeatedly negotiate with the Anhui Provincial Government. The bridges south of Tongcheng will be repaired by the Construction Department, and temporary bridges will be built north of Tongcheng for temporary traffic. The road was officially opened to traffic on October 25th. The above three lines are all the result of military-civilian cooperation. Zhufou'an, 40 li away from Huoshan, is a producing area of tea, bamboo and timber in western Anhui. The department is now building a branch line directly to Huoshan, which will be completed at the beginning of next month, and uses Maotanchang as the transshipment wharf for tea, bamboo and timber in western Anhui, 35 li away from the Shanwang River in the western section of the Shu-Huo Road. The department is also building a branch line, which can be completed at the beginning of next month. After the completion of the above three roads, transportation in western Anhui can be directly connected to the An-He Road, which will greatly help the development of the rural economy. (November 21st)

Regulations for Jiangsu Province on Conscripting Labor for Dredging Rivers

Detailed Rules for Implementation Passed by the Provincial Government Meeting

Zhenjiang Communication: The Jiangsu Province Conscription Regulations for Dredging Rivers were previously passed by the Provincial Committee Meeting. Subsequently, the Construction Department, based on the regulations, drafted detailed rules for implementation, which were revised by the Compilation and Review Committee and were also approved by the Provincial Government yesterday. The detailed rules consist of 57 articles, which stipulate in detail the methods for implementing conscripted labor for dredging rivers. The main points are selected as follows: ㈠ All earthwork for dredging rivers included in the conscription plan, such as removing soil from the river and building embankments and roadbeds, shall be carried out by conscripted labor. ㈡ The period for conscripted labor for dredging rivers shall be carried out during the winter and spring seasons when the water dries up and farmers are free from agricultural work, unless otherwise specifically stipulated. ㈢ For rivers to be dredged within the boundaries of each county, the county government shall supervise the Construction Bureau to conduct surveys first in accordance with the standard rules issued by the department, and submit a plan with diagrams, earthwork tables, and explanations for approval. ㈣ Each county shall conscript labor for dredging rivers to a length of 100 to 300 kilometers per year. ㈤ Trunk rivers spanning two or more counties shall be dredged once every five years. Trunk rivers within the county that are related to water conservancy and transportation shall be dredged once every three years, and branch rivers and field ditches shall be dredged once a year. ㈥ Anyone who has already been conscripted for labor in one place in the same year may be exempted from the same type of conscripted labor in other places. ㈦ The working hours are stipulated as eight hours per day. ㈧ Temporarily, cultivated land within 20 li on both sides of the river within the river basin shall be considered within the scope of conscripted labor. ㈨ Tenant farmers shall use the labor force provided by the tenant's household as the standard for distribution. When loans are used instead of labor, they shall be distributed according to the ratio of 60% for the landowner and 40% for the tenant. ㈩ For cultivated land within the river basin, a household with 50 mu of land shall use every 10 mu as a conscription unit (households with one mu or more of self-cultivated land or two mu or more of tenant cultivated land, but less than 10 mu, shall be counted as a unit) to calculate the standard for distributing conscripted labor or loans. (For example, if the total amount of conscripted labor for the benefited cultivated land of a certain river is 5,000 workdays, and there are 500 conscription units, then each unit shall provide two workers. If the total amount of conscripted labor is the same as above, and there are 10,000 conscription units, then every two units shall provide one worker. ㈩㈠ In the river basin, men who are two years or more residents, from the age of 18 to 45, are considered able-bodied men and have the obligation to be conscripted. ㈩㈡ Industries that utilize the river for shipping, salt transport, and commerce shall jointly bear a certain percentage of the total project, the percentage of which shall be temporarily agreed upon by the County River Dredging Association and the relevant agencies and organizations. ㈩㈢ Households with no able-bodied men or with able-bodied men who cannot be conscripted may hire workers to replace them according to the apportioned amount. Industries such as salt affairs, shipping, and commerce, which bear a share of the project, may use cash instead of labor if they are unwilling to provide labor. ㈩㈣ Poor households with no able-bodied men (households with less land than a unit) and poor households with only one able-bodied man who is the sole provider for the family shall be exempted from conscription. ㈩㈤ Poor households in barren areas who are directly affected by floods and have suffered crop failures of 70% or more may be given food rations, with the price not exceeding four dimes per cubic meter, based on the standard of extreme poverty unable to provide for themselves. ㈩㈥ The county government shall dispatch police teams to maintain order in the work area and prevent bandits from mixing in and inciting trouble. Adequate sanitary and medical facilities should be provided. Workers who become ill may stop working, but must make up the work after recovery. If squad and platoon leaders are abusive, they should be reported at any time. ㈩㈦ Industries such as shipping, salt affairs, and commerce that have special relations and voluntarily bear a larger percentage or provide extra labor, and households that have been exempted from labor and voluntarily provide labor for conscription shall be given preferential rewards. Personnel who engage in embezzlement and violate orders shall be severely punished according to law. (November 22nd)

Local Communications

Kunshan

Military Police Commits Suicide in Hotel: Gu Li, a soldier of the Second Machine Gun Company of the Fifth Regiment of the Military Police currently stationed at Chongfa Temple in Changzhou and a native of Changshu, was recently ordered by his superiors to go to Shanghai to purchase goods. Unfortunately, he lost all the silver dollars he was carrying on the tram and was unable to return to camp. He went to Kunshan and stayed in room number 8 of the Zhengtai Hotel. At midnight, he secretly swallowed opium and committed suicide. Yesterday morning, Gu called the waiter to make water. The waiter entered the room and noticed something unusual in Gu's face, knowing that he had taken poison. He quickly reported to the cashier and sent Gu by car to Guangren Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, the poison has entered his limbs and it is difficult to predict whether his life can be saved. There are four letters left behind, addressed to his superiors and family.

Jiangyin

Liu Zaigeng Arrested and Escorted to Wujin: Liu Zaigeng, the former Sixth District Chief and Commander, and the garrison special service company of the Huangtu Town fortress in the district, and the Fourth Company of the Second Regiment of Military Police stationed in Changzhou, jointly suppressed bandits in Baizhang Town, Wujin County on October 3, 1930. Peng Quanlin was shot dead on the spot by Di Rongfa, a soldier of the fortress. Later, his brother Peng Jinkang filed a case in Wujin accusing Liu of killing innocent people. Two years have passed. Yesterday (22nd), the county government suddenly received a secret order from the Civil Affairs Department, ordering the police to arrest Liu. After a brief interrogation, it was decided to escort him to the Wujin County Court for trial on the 23rd.

Wuxi

Long-Distance Traveler Visits Wuxi for Investigation: Sun Leshan, the number one long-distance traveler in Anhui, is passionate about cultural undertakings. He personally went to various provinces, cities, and counties across the country for on-site investigation, introducing them to various counties. This trip is expected to take six years. He arrived in Wuxi from Wujin the night before, and has been visiting various educational institutions in the county in recent days, collecting valuable materials for reference in his writings. According to Sun, his inspection purpose is mainly focused on rural villages, because the rural village environment is different, which can be good materials for various places. The local People's Education Center specially invited Sun to give a speech on the social conditions of various places at 3 pm yesterday (22nd).

Nantong

Bandits in Dongchengkou Resist Arrest: At 11 pm on the 21st, there were five or six bandits in the new market in Dongchengkou. They encountered a patrol police team. Because they refused inspection, the two sides opened fire. At that time, the gunshots were very loud, pedestrians ran away, and the order was in chaos. As a result, one bandit was killed and a box gun was seized. The people in the city did not know the truth and were frightened. The military and police temporarily imposed martial law. The dead bandit was examined by the court on the morning of the 22nd.

Collection of land survey fee has been stopped: The land survey fee of Tongyi has been collected along with the land price tax and has collected 110,000 yuan. The county government has now presented it to the provincial land bureau and the collection will be stopped this year.

Zhenjiang

Construction Department Rectifies Inland Water Launches: The Jiangsu Construction Department believes that water transport in each county is very important. There are many inland water launches that have disrepaired hulls and outdated machines. They cannot guarantee the safety of passengers, nor can they accurately adhere to the schedule and limit the number of passengers, which greatly affects travel safety. Yesterday, it specifically notified the construction bureaus of each county to thoroughly investigate and report the plan to the department for approval.

Yangzhou

Tongfuxiang Salt Shop Robbed of Huge Sum: On the morning of the 21st, Tongfuxiang Salt Shop in Shaobo sent Wang Yongfa, a shop clerk, and two patrol team soldiers, Xu Zhengguo and Zhu Zhengzhong, carrying box cannons, to escort a sum of 6,541 yuan by boat to Yangzhou. When passing near the Guanyin Hall on the west bank of Wayao Shop River, they encountered seven or eight bandits in gray uniforms and wearing badges, carrying three pistols. They ordered the boat to stop and swarmed aboard, first disarming the escorts, and then taking the money.

Gaoyou

Chief of Tax Collection Accused of Embezzling Taxes: Feng Jinyang, the former Chief of Tax Collection in this county, was accused of embezzling a huge amount of national taxes. County Chief Li ordered the grain clerk Fan Jiazhen and others to check the books, totaling 6,581.972 yuan and 190,782 yuan of cash embezzled in 17 years. The grain clerk had reported the case. Now, because the county government is silent about the case, they filed another report with the county government, requesting strict handling in accordance with the law.

Teachers' Demand for Salaries Continues: Yesterday (20th), all the teachers in the city pushed the representatives Gao Fusun and others to request salaries from the county government. After consultation, they agreed to pay 4,000 yuan on the 27th and 3,000 yuan on October. At 2 pm, all the teachers were still gathered in the girls' primary school. They are satisfied with the amount of payment, but they discussed the issue of old debts for several hours, and decided to restore the previous soil club to handle the debt recovery matters.

Taixian

Disturbance Occurs Due to the Collection of Business Tax: Hong Lvzhi, the Director of the Business Tax Bureau of Taidong and Haian counties, and Guo, an official, went to Haian Town in the county on the morning of the 18th to collect business tax. He was involved in a tax amount dispute with Huaxing General Merchandise Store and a conflict broke out. Hong, in his anger, sent the store owner to the Public Security Bureau for punishment to warn others. For a time, the people gathered to express their grievances, and all the stores sent representatives to the Chamber of Commerce to petition. At the same time, all the stores went on strike. The Director and the members of the team saw that the turmoil had been aroused, and they returned to the apartment in succession and notified the Public Security Bureau to suppress the unrest. Unexpectedly, some people followed behind to inquire about the news, and saw Guo, an official of the Business Tax Bureau, smoking opium pellets in the apartment. They immediately broke into the door, seized the smoking paraphernalia, and handed them to the Director of the Public Security Bureau, and demanded disposal on the spot. The Director of the Bureau took the equipment and Guo to the bureau for investigation on site, under his authority. Director Hong saw that the storm was expanding, and that evening he has fled to other places to avoid the punishment.
