Film Essays

Poor and Arduous Practice When People Aren't Looking

— Chen Dabei

The fundamental way to learn a foreign language is to first memorize the alphabet, and then one can spell words and read books. The fundamental way to learn dramatic expression is also similar. One must first take the simplest emotions as units, practice them one by one until they are mature, and then one can further practice complex expressions.

As mentioned earlier, before you practice the following expressions, you must prepare a large mirror that can reflect your whole body (whether it is a folding dressing mirror or a dressing mirror on a wardrobe is fine). If your economic ability cannot afford it, or you cannot close the door to practice quietly in the place where that large mirror is placed, then it is best to hang a mirror that can reflect your whole face on the wall in a room where you can practice alone. It is best to have it at the same height as your eyes when you are standing. If you can't do that either, you can always find a target about the size of a nail head at the height of your eyes when you are standing in a place where you can practice alone. When you practice alone, you may as well concentrate your gaze on that target. The results obtained from this kind of poor and arduous practice may be more powerful than the results of practicing in front of a large dressing mirror in a large Western-style house. To be honest, the teacher can only teach you a method. Success is created by the student's own strong will and perseverance.

However, one point must be noted. If your concentrated target is any object other than the mirror, you must often look for opportunities outside of practice, and when people are not prepared, practice the few expressions you have already practiced in front of the mirror once or twice. As long as you don't deliberately attract the attention of others, maybe others won't notice you. Haven't you seen some people who often like to raise their eyebrows and glare their eyes in front of the mirror? As long as you don't explain that you are concentrating on practicing a skill there, jealous ridicule and scolding may not be triggered.

Film Review

Review of *High Pressure*

— Yannan

*High Pressure*, which premiered at the Cathay yesterday, is William Powell's first work for Warner Bros. after leaving Paramount. The story can be said to be very ordinary; it can also be said to be very complex, and the business it depicts is indeed often seen in culturally advanced cities. This kind of business is the so-called "slick business". Its reality everywhere satirizes those large stores/companies that are strong on the outside but empty on the inside: only caring about the facade; and the goods they operate, apart from the "sample rooms" used to decorate some, are actually empty. It scolds those nominal stores and blind investors. But the so-called inside story is not that much.

In addition, it also sketches the jealousy and infighting of the same industry. These are unavoidable and undeniable treacherous facts in the economic society. Also, the modern popular vanity disease, especially among women, is also shown in detail.

William Powell is still the William Powell of the past. He is very experienced in playing a shrewd and sinister businessman: a thoughtful and steady attitude that no one in Hollywood can match. George Sidney plays a very heavy role in this film, but he handles it with ease and serves as a good assistant to William. As for the rest of the people, there is nothing to talk about: they are merely competent. The photographic lighting is also mediocre.

Many of the interspersed scenes are similar to "hard comedy": of course, this is a goal of Warner Bros. films (short comedies). But they are not unreasonable or annoying, but make people feel happier.

Its problem is that there is too much dialogue about "business experience" (the pronunciation is very good), which makes the scene a bit deserted. The ending seems finished but not finished. Although the flashback is not bad, it will definitely cause people's dissatisfaction.

In short, it is a film that capitalists or businessmen must see!

Reader Opinions

Shoot a Film of the Bloody Battle of the Volunteer Army

— Daosheng

In the past six months, many cinemas operated by Chinese nationals in this city have been showing war films about the January 28th Incident, such as *The Anti-Japanese War History of the 19th Route Army*, *A Soldier of the 19th Route Army*, and *The Bloody Battle of Shanghai*. These films can undoubtedly attract the general public.

Lost My Lover with a Car

— Buwu

Rapper Fando is back in Hollywood! Guess what she brought back? A brand-new Duesenberg car; a very gorgeous black sable fur coat; and many beautiful and precious rubies.

Rapper said: "None of the men in Hollywood can arouse my interest." In fact, she has taken a fancy to Bert Taylor. She had to leave New York and her lover because she wanted to go to Hollywood to shoot a new film.

Audience, and on the one hand it can excite the emotions of the audience, giving a strong and tragic stimulus. These films have not failed to help in the salvation of the national crisis. But I think it is not enough, and there is further expectation.

My opinion... I hope that major domestic film companies will quickly produce several films about the bloody battles of the Northeast Volunteer Army. The heroic and mighty spirit of the Northeast Volunteer Army, the arduous and extraordinary struggle of the Northeast Volunteer Army, how they fought hand-to-hand with stubborn enemies in the wilderness or mountains, how they fought great battles in single clothes in the ice and snow: all kinds of spirits of fighting and sacrificing for the country should be captured on camera and made active on the screen. Even if it is not possible to actually go to the Northeast Volunteer Army's position for production, efforts should be made to make it lifelike, and the more tragic it is, the better.

In fact, in this time of serious national crisis, all hot-blooded blockbusters, song and dance blockbusters, and films that play around with love are empty dramas that do not help the facts, and are only for the wealthy and leisurely classes to enjoy. What is most needed now are films that can uplift the national spirit.

Celebrity Mini-History

A Short Biography of Martial Arts Star Cha Ruilong

— Shi Mengyuan

Martial arts star Cha Ruilong is a native of Dinghai, Zhejiang. He was born and raised in Shanghai. At the age of fourteen, he enrolled in the Shanggong Primary School, affiliated with the Commercial Press. He enjoyed practicing martial arts from a young age. Li Weisheng, the school's Chinese martial arts instructor, greatly admired him and provided him with dedicated guidance. After graduation, he studied at Cheng Tian Middle School. However, he dropped out due to other reasons shortly after and pursued a career in architecture. This was not his passion, and he would practice martial arts whenever he had free time. Later, he became a disciple of the old boxing master Tong Zhongyi of Cangzhou. Within four years, his skills greatly improved. He participated in martial arts competitions at the Universal Sports Association and defeated all his opponents. Spectators were amazed by his bravery.

At that time, a Westerner wanted to take Cha abroad, but Cha refused, believing the offer lacked sincerity. Later, he gathered several like-minded individuals and founded the National Martial Arts Research Association, inviting his master Tong Zhongyi to serve as the head coach. He also served as the director of the martial arts department at the Commercial Press, nurturing many talents. In the seventeenth year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1928], when the Northern Expeditionary Army arrived in Shanghai, the film industry held a theatrical performance to entertain the Northern Expeditionary generals and soldiers. Cha joined the performance and became famous throughout Shanghai for his unique skills. Later, he served as the director of the martial arts department at the Yueming Film Company, co-starring with Wu Lizhu in "The Hero of Guandong," achieving remarkable success and earning high praise from the public. He is only in his early twenties and looks like a refined scholar. Those who do not know him would hardly believe he is the powerful Cha Ruilong.

Movie World News

Janet Gaynor's Latest Decision Regarding Her Acting Style

— Wang Zhiji

Janet Gaynor thought that she was capable of playing not only lively, innocent girls, but also the roles that Norma Shearer, Constance Bennett, Joan Crawford, and others could play. Therefore, she repeatedly resolved to change her acting style; however, she has now abandoned her proposition.

Starting with her successful film "Seventh Heaven," she continued to play roles, whether she was playing a cute girl-next-door or a lonely orphan; she was always a lovable "Diana." After her success, she became fickle and wanted to change her acting style.

The film company complied with her wishes and gave her a

Page 22

Shen Bao Local Supplement

film called "The Man Who Comes Back," but it failed. She had lost her lovable spirit on screen!

Despite the failure, she remained determined not to continue with the "Janet Gaynor style" of acting. Critics said she had to maintain the style she had in "Seventh Heaven," but she ignored them.

Recently, Fox Film Corporation bought a script for her, "Rebecca of Sunnybrook Farm." The character Rebecca was most suitable for her personality; however, she was unwilling to take it on. She took "The First Year of Marriage," which was originally intended for Sally Eilers and James Dunn, and the script that the company had intended for her was given to Marlene Dietrich.

Although the premiere is still far away, people returning from the filming location say that Marlene's performance is no less impressive than Janet's.

Marlene is not the only one competing with Janet; Lilian Harvey, who came to Hollywood from Europe, is also competing with Janet. Lilian previously received the same kind of praise as Janet for her performance in "Congress Dances."

Ronald Colman Is Also Afraid of Death, Having Taken Out a Life Insurance Policy for One Million Dollars

— Lin

Ronald Colman's "Movie Crazy" opened today at the Grand and Nanking theaters simultaneously. Because filming this movie involved many dangers, he took out a life insurance policy for a total of one million dollars. He said that the value of a person's life is inestimable; therefore, a person's insurance should be as high as possible without limitation. Ronald Colman's one-million-dollar insurance policy is not the highest in the American film industry because Will Rogers, John Barrymore, Charlie Chaplin, Douglas Fairbanks, Bessie Love and others all have life insurance policies worth over one million dollars.

Many people say that Sally Eilers and James Dunn may film "Janet-style" movies and succeed. At the same time, Joan Bennett also intends to make a "Janet-style" movie.

Janet wants to preserve her past glory and stand above those who imitate her style. At the same time, because of public criticism, she has been asked to retain her previous style. Therefore, she has decided to abandon her intention to change her style and continue playing the kind of innocent, lively, and blossoming young woman. Therefore, we will soon be able to see the Janet of "Seventh Heaven" again.

Movie Trivia

John Gilbert's Cunning Plan

— Xin

A year ago, John Gilbert felt that his position was wavering. Many audiences no longer supported him, and some even scolded or ridiculed him. The film company tried its best to find out why a big star who had been praised for years was suddenly rejected. However, there was no way to remedy the situation, and no one knew the reason why.

Later, John discovered the reason himself. He wrote a novel in which he made himself the protagonist, saying, "He is a very sinister person whose behavior is extremely cunning. He is so bad that he is rejected by society." This novel became popular in the United States and received good reviews. After reading it, audiences liked him again because he admitted his own cunning.

Now he has returned to the peak of his former glory and is loved by audiences. But no one would have thought that loving him was precisely falling for his cunning plan.

What Does Your First Time Taste Like?

— Xing

Edna May Oliver has never kissed anyone on screen before. But in the new film "Hold 'Em Jail," she made an exception and held her "first screen kiss" ceremony.

Just Chatting

Why Do People Like Watching Foreign Movies?

— Xidiao

Perhaps this is not a question worth discussing for you all. Why do people like watching foreign movies? Actually, this is indeed a question worth discussing.

In our country, which lacks investigation and statistics, there are of course no investigations or statistics regarding how many foreign films are imported each year, and how much money flies into the pockets of foreigners without them lifting a finger. However, everyone knows that the number is surprisingly large.

I once asked many friends in the education sector, and they only responded with giggles. It seemed that they had forgotten that movies are a tool of public education because this was something outside of their jurisdiction.

Yesterday, I unintentionally chatted with a friend about this question that had been lingering in my mind for a long time. Thanks to his guidance, he gave me a clear answer. Ah, from this I know that it all comes from the gifts of our education.

Everyone knows that in our schools, we almost disdain studying Chinese; while we happen to take the opposite stance towards English. Starting from middle school, students will buy some English books, and at the same time, everyone will put on a navy blue serge Western suit that seems to make them look like a young gigolo. Having understood English and wearing a Western suit, even if one's English is not fluent, one will still say a few sentences in "pidgin English." Everything else must also try to catch up with foreigners. For the sake of practical research, watching foreign movies is a good move from several perspectives. Haha! Isn't this the reason?

Editor's Note: This may be one of many reasons, but it should not be generalized.

Greta Garbo's Mourning After Paul Bern's Suicide

— Meicun

Paul Bern's sudden suicide was a shock that Hollywood had never experienced. He was a film producer and the husband of actress Jean Harlow. He died on September 6th, only two months after they were married! Paul was one of Hollywood's most fashionable figures. Because of his generosity and frequent assistance to others in need, he earned the title "The Kindest Hearted Man in a Heartless Town." More than a thousand people came to offer flowers at his memorial service. Since her husband's death, it was generally said by Hollywood colleagues and outsiders that Jean Harlow's film life would come to a halt, but Jean was not discouraged. She admired Billie Burke's courage (Billie continued to film "A Bill of Divorcement" after her husband Florenz Ziegfeld's death). Therefore, she also continued filming "Red Dust." (The male lead is Clark Gable). However, the sadness she felt was too deep, so on her first day back to filming, a special nurse was assigned to carefully watch over her, to prevent her nerves from collapsing. Her stepfather, Marino Bello, also often followed her closely, to prevent accidents. Now she is gradually recovering, and the film is progressing smoothly.

Theater Knowledge

The Three Bad Habits of Moviegoers in Theaters

— Bin

1. Reading Subtitles Aloud: Most people who go to the movies are literate. However, some moviegoers who know a few words like to pretend to be smart. When they see the subtitles on the screen, they hum and read them aloud like an old woman chanting scriptures! This makes the audience in the surrounding seats unable to concentrate on watching the movie. Therefore, in American movie theaters, there is a regulation that those who read subtitles aloud will be charged with disturbing the peace and fined twenty-five US dollars. As a result, order in American movie theaters is very quiet, without any noisy sounds.

2. Inappropriate Jeering: Sometimes, when a movie has been shown many times, or it is an old film, it is often interrupted halfway through the showing. Therefore, when the audience is watching something interesting, they become annoyed by the interruption. Some idlers even boo loudly, and even clap their hands and stomp their feet, causing the order to fall into a state of unrest. The reason for this is partly because the film is too old, or the operator is negligent, and partly because the audience has no sense of public morality.

3. Leaving Before It's Over: It seems that everyone who goes to the movies is a busy person. Why is that? Because when the movie is about to end but hasn't finished, they all stand up one after another in preparation to leave, preventing the audience in the back rows from seeing! The reason for this is probably that some moviegoers have read the synopsis beforehand and know that a certain scene is about to end, so they stand up and leave first. While this is probably correct, it seems inappropriate to obstruct the view of others.
